  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_88f76453-ac4f-4b27-8a0a-f88fd2082425'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer14865798488224329512"><b>My name is Gin, and I kill people.</b><br/><br/>They call me the Spider.   <span id="freeText14865798488224329512" style="display:none"><b>My name is Gin, and I kill people.</b><br /><br />They call me the Spider. I'm the most feared assassin in the South — when I'm not busy at the Pork Pit cooking up the best barbecue in Ashland. As a Stone elemental, I can hear everything from the whispers of the gravel beneath my feet to the vibrations of the soaring Appalachian Mountains above me. My Ice magic also comes in handy for making the occasional knife. But I don't use my powers on the job unless I absolutely have to. Call it professional pride.<br /><br />Now that a ruthless Air elemental has double-crossed me and killed my handler, I'm out for revenge. And I'll exterminate anyone who gets in my way — good or bad. I may look hot, but I'm still one of the bad guys. Which is why I'm in trouble, since irresistibly rugged Detective Donovan Caine has agreed to help me. The last thing this coldhearted killer needs when I'm battling a magic more powerful than my own is a sexy distraction... especially when Donovan wants me dead just as much as the enemy.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351673044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6688427790019388090"><b>9/30/17 - ON SALE for $2.99:</b> <br/><br/><a href='https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B0033CS69Y/ref=as_li_ss_il?caller=Goodreads&callerLink=https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6611038-spider-s-bite?from_search=true&linkCode=li1&tag=rabrea-20&linkId=c273bd48e8d80e036c72a1c3cea3448c' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468937429i/19761488.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468937429i/19761489.gif' width='1' height='1' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.to/2yf0RGH'>http://amzn.to/2yf0RGH</a><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>So here's the thing about ELEMENTAL ASSASSIN: it's a great urban fantasy series.<br/><br/>It really is. <br/><br/>The magic system is complex and interesting, the setting is cool, the secondary characters are sympathetic and easy to connect with, and Gin . . . well, Gin is a stone-cold killer (HA!).<br/><br/>That being said, this first installment (like so many others) has a few problems. <br/><br/>BUT. With a very few exceptions, most of the things that bug me about Gin </span>
  <span id="freeText6688427790019388090" style="display:none"><b>9/30/17 - ON SALE for $2.99:</b> <br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B0033CS69Y/ref=as_li_ss_il?caller=Goodreads&amp;callerLink=https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6611038-spider-s-bite?from_search=true&amp;linkCode=li1&amp;tag=rabrea-20&amp;linkId=c273bd48e8d80e036c72a1c3cea3448c" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468937429i/19761488.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468937429i/19761489.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/2yf0RGH">http://amzn.to/2yf0RGH</a><br><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>So here's the thing about ELEMENTAL ASSASSIN: it's a great urban fantasy series.<br><br>It really is. <br><br>The magic system is complex and interesting, the setting is cool, the secondary characters are sympathetic and easy to connect with, and Gin . . . well, Gin is a stone-cold killer (HA!).<br><br>That being said, this first installment (like so many others) has a few problems. <br><br>BUT. With a very few exceptions, most of the things that bug me about Gin (or whatever), are the reverse of something I love about her (or whatever). <br><br>I can never know for sure whether an author does this on purpose, but I can't help but treat it less harshly than I would if it didn't have that aspect of realism--I'm one of those "THE BOOKS ARE REAL! THE PEOPLE ARE REAL!" type readers.<br><br>YES, I know they aren't really real, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[don't be a dick <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but while I'm reading, if the author has done her job, it <i>feels</i> real. <br><br>And in real relationships, *coughs* like my marriage *coughs* and my family *coughs* the things that drive you the most crazy about a person, are byproducts of the same things you love the most.<br><br>For example, Gin went through some very dark times in her childhood. It's given her a wry sense of humor, and she views life sans anything resembling rose-colored glasses. Her reality is often bleak, but Estep gives it a haunting beauty:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I grimaced at his grandiose tone. Sometimes Fletcher reminded me of a circus ringmaster making the sad elephants, browbeaten horses, and two-bit acts seem more thrilling than they actually were.</i>
</blockquote><br>Alternately, she sometimes has TERRIBLE fashion sense:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Tight black jeans, leather jacket, boots, and a long-sleeved, black T-shirt <b>with a pair of sequined cherries on the front.</b></i>
</blockquote><br>Her outfit before that involved a t-shirt with blackberries, cut so low the edge of her bra was on display.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427991078i/14347821.jpg" width="400" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But Gin isn't the kind of girl to pay close attention to fashion, and that's one of the things that I love about her, so I cringe and move on. In real life, I'd take her to the mall and help an assassin out. <br><br>This also happens with her Southernisms. It's a toss up as to whether I'm going to get one that makes me laugh in fond remembrance:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Nope, it’s chicory coffee.” Finn raised his own mug in salute. “It’ll put hair on your chest.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Or shudder b/c CRASS:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i> . . . the balance was off, and the wooden handle was slick as hot shit in the summertime, but it would do the job.</i>
</blockquote><br>Most of the time, a few statements like that are enough to lose a star, but when an author is able to make it feel consistent with the character's personality, I give it a pass. <br><br>So that's Gin. <br><br>We're only just beginning to meet her support system: her adopted brother Finnegan Lane, and dwarve sisters Jo Jo and Sophia Deveraux. <br><br>Not much to say about Jo Jo and Sophia yet, beyond both of their elemental gifts being extremely helpful, but Finn . . . I loved Finn instantly:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Maybe, maybe not. You know my thoughts on honest men.” <br>“That there aren’t any.” <br>Finn shot his forefinger at me. “Precisely.”</i>
</blockquote><br>My interpretation of Ashland is that Estep picked up one of the big Southern cities--Atlanta, Montgomery, Nashville, etc.--and plopped it down in Asheville. I have no idea how accurate that is, but that's what it feels like to me. <br><br>It's old school Southern, and Estep being a Southerner herself, it's authentic. But it's not the refined, whitewashed South. Oh, there are the bejeweled women in flouncy dresses and the men in seersucker suits, but Gin is an ASSASSIN. For her cover, works as a waitress at a dive restaurant called the Pork Pit. <br><br>And sometimes all the thugs and Gin's interactions with them feel more like Prohibition era Chicago than Tara. But, <i>again</i>, I like that.<br><br>SO. If you're a fan of urban fantasy, and looking for a quick, fun read, you should definitely add ELEMENTAL ASSASSIN to your TBR. SPIDER'S BITE is a solid first installment, and it only gets better from here. Plus, you know, ASSASSIN. <br><br><b>Pre-review:</b><br><br>If there was an "s" or two in "Donovan Caine," I'd be willing to spend HOURS trying to rearrange the letters to spell "self-righteous prick."<br><br>And then I'd drink some blackberry lemonade to celebrate.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_127076313" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127076313" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127076313?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8176904-spider-s-bite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=romance-romance-romance">romance-romance-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127076313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1598184001416815405">The PNR genre has certainly grown a great deal in the past few years, but nothing much has changed.<br/><br/>It still draws a helluva lot of inspiration from Buffy. And who wouldn't? Buffy was hot. Buffy was funny. Buffy kicked arse. <br/><br/>Thankfully Estep's main character, Gin, isn't that funny but she does kick a lot of arse. Often and without all that pesky remorse that most other female protagonists are forced to endure by their cruel creators. <br/><br/>Because remorse is like an STD, folks, you get it by getting cl</span>
  <span id="freeText1598184001416815405" style="display:none">The PNR genre has certainly grown a great deal in the past few years, but nothing much has changed.<br /><br />It still draws a helluva lot of inspiration from Buffy. And who wouldn't? Buffy was hot. Buffy was funny. Buffy kicked arse. <br /><br />Thankfully Estep's main character, Gin, isn't that funny but she does kick a lot of arse. Often and without all that pesky remorse that most other female protagonists are forced to endure by their cruel creators. <br /><br />Because remorse is like an STD, folks, you get it by getting close to people, it never goes away and it makes you a lot less fun to be with when you're not on your medication. <br /><br />The novel was refreshingly free of duo love interests competing for our protagonist’s affections. You can imagine, after reading so many PNR romances and Urban fantasy novels, that I’m about to gorge out my own eyes before watching two men pussy foot around the same arse-kicking wench until she finally chooses the wrong one. (Penny will agree with me – she always roots for the underdog!)<br /><br />I would say that my one complaint about this novel is Estep’s heroizing (no, not a ‘real’ word but really, if we all pitch in together then we can MAKE it a real word!) Gin. This chick is an assassin and she never kills a single person in this book that doesn’t thoroughly deserve it. Thoroughly. Estep actually goes to great pains to ensure that we know that every single person knifed or otherwise stabbed (she doesn’t always stab with knives so I don’t want you to confuse the two, folks!) deserves it.<br /><br />Let’s face it, the majority of her clients are NOT child molester’s and rapists and thugs who get off on torturing people. The majority of her clients are probably stock-brokers or politicians or supreme court judges or some such ilk who haven’t done too much wrong other than pissing off the wrong people.<br /><br />Look, if you’re going to make your main character a cold hearted bitch – that’s actually okay with me. I can relate to that! But don’t tell us she’ll kill anything (except for children apparently) for a paycheck and then have her only kill bad guys in the actual text. Be brave. Go all out, Estep! I’m actually pretty confident you could pull it off!<br /><br />This world does have vampires and long-lived dwarves in it but the main paranormal focus comes from the various elemental magic users which is a nice change of pace from the norm. Vampires aren’t even that awesome in this novel. Cool, I’m down with that. It’s not like Dracula was too much of a badass. I mean, c’mon, Van Helsing and co. weren’t exactly the brightest bulbs on the Christmas tree as far as a Scooby gang goes.<br /> <br />The writing was smooth, the action was well paced and I enjoyed Gin’s forward and confident nature in dealing with the world around her and with Detective Caine who could stand to pull the stick out of his ass but was otherwise a good love interest and main character.<br /><br />I will read the rest of this series until it either ends or I get bored. It was interesting and well written enough to keep me around but I wouldn’t say it’s a shining beacon of awesome in the genre like Mind Games was. Then again, what is there to expect? Like the hookers in this book, the PNR genre is getting a little old, a little tired, and looking a little more frayed around the edges. Maybe it’s time for the old girl to call it quits.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1598184001416815405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1506363562" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1506363562" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1506363562?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=paranormal-mystery">paranormal-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=yay-feminism">yay-feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1506363562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13313956396706923000"><b>
  <i>The sentimental part of me was dead, burned away and crumbled to ash -- just like my family had been.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Yep, it's that good. I have to give the book points for seriously putting out every cheesy line and stereotype that could possibly be used in this story. We had the bad-ass assassin girl who was out on the streets as a kid until a kind-hearted assassin took her in and trained her to kill. Now, she is the most feared assassin around and kills without regret. But, only people who deserve to be </span>
  <span id="freeText13313956396706923000" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>The sentimental part of me was dead, burned away and crumbled to ash -- just like my family had been.</i>
</b><br><br>Yep, it's that good. I have to give the book points for seriously putting out every cheesy line and stereotype that could possibly be used in this story. We had the bad-ass assassin girl who was out on the streets as a kid until a kind-hearted assassin took her in and trained her to kill. Now, she is the most feared assassin around and kills without regret. But, only people who deserve to be killed. No kids, pets, or torturing. She has a code. They always have a code.... Well, guess what? I have a code too. If you write crap like this:<br><br><b>
  <i>Part of me wanted to punch him in his nose. Another part of me wanted to pull him toward me, plant my lips on his...</i>
</b><br><br>my code is telling me to give you a low rating. My code also doesn't allow for stereotyping that says these things:<br><br><i>
  <b>..ditched the glasses in a dumpster next to a Chinese restaurant. The metal container reeked of soy sauce and week-old fried rice...<br><br>Several good ole boys chain-smoked and knocked back beers on their front stoops, while inside, their wives hurried to put dinner on the table in time to avoid getting a fresh shiner....<br><br>A couple of blocks over, a vampire hooker would do you in your car for fifty bucks, while the homeless guys dug through trash cans looking for enough garbage to eat for the night.<br><br>I hoped the police force was stocked up on coffee and doughnuts because the body count was about to go up tonight.<br><br>If there was one thing all southern women instinctively know how to do, it's flirt. It's encoded in our DNA, along with a fondness for grease, sugar, and oversize hats...</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448073342i/17091325.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay - enough!! My code has a huge problem with those quotes. And, that's not even scratching the surface of the giant block of (possibly racist) cheese. She also says that she has to "lullaby" a guy, and that when they are about to fight, that then they "dance". Seriously? I rolled my eyes so many times that they got stuck that way - just like my mother warned me.<br><br>So, basically, this book is ridiculous. Which is a bummer because the premise and the world is cool. It just couldn't deliver the same originality in the story. It was this fresh idea wrapped in an old, worn-out wrapper. Like a day-old, half-eaten, eggroll that was probably in that dumpster behind the Chinese restaurant.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439137043ra/15799466.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13313956396706923000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=uf-pnr">uf-pnr</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1626773439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11318631340563961127">BUDDY READ!!! With my UF girls at <a>Buddies Books and Baubles</a><br/><br/>Female Assassin....I'm totally in.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462192394i/18964147.jpg' width='400' height='284' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>My favorite thing about this book was the fact Gin was a pretty sexually aggressive woman who wasn’t even close to the near virginal heroine that I usually see in a UF series. I appreciate that because while I usually don’t mind that trope so much it is refreshing to have a woman who is really secure in her sexuality running around no matter if we need to read about how wet her who-ha is on multiple occ</span>
  <span id="freeText11318631340563961127" style="display:none">BUDDY READ!!! With my UF girls at <a>Buddies Books and Baubles</a><br><br>Female Assassin....I'm totally in.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462192394i/18964147.jpg" width="400" height="284" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>My favorite thing about this book was the fact Gin was a pretty sexually aggressive woman who wasn’t even close to the near virginal heroine that I usually see in a UF series. I appreciate that because while I usually don’t mind that trope so much it is refreshing to have a woman who is really secure in her sexuality running around no matter if we need to read about how wet her who-ha is on multiple occasions. Besides most of the time she is running around killing people or planning on killing people so it is a fair trade in my book<br><blockquote>
  <i>“You're late."<br>"Sorry. I was busy talking about my feelings and killing people.” </i>
</blockquote><br>This is a pretty basic introductory book. I have a pretty good notion of how the world works. There is Gin who basically can control/listen to rocks, has a heart of stone and kills people for a living. She is pretty likable right off the bat as she has a little bit of an attitude that she likes to throw around. I like that in a heroine<br><br>Gin comes complete with a horrible tragedy in her past and a kooky set of friends and work acquaintances to lighten the drama. Finn was one of my favorites. I love that they have a rapport like siblings….squabling and fighting in a fun way that shows all the love and affection they have for each other. Sure they might have gotten sweaty together in their youths but now they are the best of friends and family to each other.<br><br>There is also a smidge of romance….well sort of. There is at least a tall dark handsome and completely wrong man for Gin in this. It was enough to give us something steamy in-between all the mayhem but a cop and an assassin…well I just don’t see that going much of anywhere in the long term.<br><blockquote>
  <i> “Maybe I find him...interesting. Attractive in an uptight sort of way. But that won't keep me from killing him if he does something stupid—like try to double-cross us. That is something thats nonnegotiable, no matter how much fuck potential he might have.” </i>
</blockquote><br>While I liked this book nothing really sticks out as extremely memorable about it. It is a good set up book and I enjoyed my time easily reading along but if I wasn’t in a buddy read for the entire series…well I might have waiting 3 months to pick up the next one. Still there is enough going on that I don’t think it will be a hardship to continue reading along with some friends.<br></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626539515" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8176904-spider-s-bite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=kick-ass-ladies">kick-ass-ladies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1626539515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4118706570998747851"><b>*** 3.44 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with the Urban Fantasy fans at BB&B!</b><br/><br/>This is a story of a girl who lost her family young, lived on the streets, met a nice family who took her in and trained her to become an assassin. And she has powers, in a world where some people are born with an ability to perform magic by controlling the elements. Gin, our hapless assassin, has control over stone, with some affinity to ice magic. However, while going about doing her job killing people, she prefers to rely on her bla</span>
  <span id="freeText4118706570998747851" style="display:none"><b>*** 3.44 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with the Urban Fantasy fans at BB&amp;B!</b><br /><br />This is a story of a girl who lost her family young, lived on the streets, met a nice family who took her in and trained her to become an assassin. And she has powers, in a world where some people are born with an ability to perform magic by controlling the elements. Gin, our hapless assassin, has control over stone, with some affinity to ice magic. However, while going about doing her job killing people, she prefers to rely on her blades and sometimes cross bow. <br /><br />We get to meet her right after she dispatches with a minor job, by this understand an easy hit, and is persuaded to embark on a very high risk, no prep, but astronomical pay new assignment. However, things are not what they seem, and hers and the lives of the people around her, are put in peril. <br /><br />I personally enjoyed the book, but I can see the validity of the arguments some of my friends have against the numerous stereotypes which plague the plot. However, I am also well aware of my personal complete acceptance of such in the different genres and take them as part of the game... So many of the series that compel us to keep on reading them are formulaic and somewhat predictable, but at least I come back exactly because of that. Sometimes it is nice that you can get out of a book exactly what you expected when you choose to buy it... It is those books that I reach for in moments when I seek comfort and running away from conflict ... <br /><br />So, despite it not being very original or exceptionally well written, this book was perfect for an enjoyable read in between the hardships of Real Life and the impending doom of the other 3 books I am reading right now, which are wonderfully crafted, but rough on my psyche and good spirit... <br /><br />I will recommend this book to fans of the lighter side of UF, including young readers, despite a love scene in which all protection was discussed and employed. It is also a first in a series and I know from experience, you have to give it 2-3 books time to grow. So, I plan on doing exactly that!<br /><br />Now I wish all of you Happy Reading and may you never be without a good book in your life!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4118706570998747851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_119244410" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119244410" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119244410?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-feb2011">zzread-feb2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119244410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9889236587278417227">Urban fantasy books are often saturated with the kick ass, snarky heroine, the requisite love interest, the paranormal creatures, cool weapons, and the evil bad guy or gal. Yes – this book has all that, but it felt like it had more. Set in the corrupt town of Ashland, Tennessee, Spider’s Bite has a dirty, gritty feel. <br/><br/>Gin Blanco is known as The Spider, a female assassin. She is extremely good at her job and is well compensated for her skills. Gin has standards, a kind of moral code. She does not</span>
  <span id="freeText9889236587278417227" style="display:none">Urban fantasy books are often saturated with the kick ass, snarky heroine, the requisite love interest, the paranormal creatures, cool weapons, and the evil bad guy or gal. Yes – this book has all that, but it felt like it had more. Set in the corrupt town of Ashland, Tennessee, Spider’s Bite has a dirty, gritty feel. <br /><br />Gin Blanco is known as The Spider, a female assassin. She is extremely good at her job and is well compensated for her skills. Gin has standards, a kind of moral code. She does not kill children or the innocent. <br /><br />I liked the originality of this book. While there are vampires in this book, their abilities are not really expanded upon, except that they seem to heal quickly. There are also giants and dwarves. There are also people that can control elemental magic – from air, fire, stone, ice, etc. Gin is an elemental. She has the ability to use stone and ice magic. While stone and ice are not the most powerful elemental magics out there, it is hinted that Gin has some extraordinary powers. I would have liked to have had more information on these elemental magic practitioners – How did they get the magic? Were they born with it? Can they learn it? <br /><br />The world building in this book was intriguing. Basically, it felt like our world but with paranormal elements. Gin lives in a corrupt city which is policed by a corrupt police force. Even the organized crime elements felt like a paranormal mafia. <br /><br />Our heroine Gin Blanco comes from tragic circumstances. Her family died in a fire, leaving her homeless. She is “found” by Fletcher, who gives her odd jobs in exchange for food. She later becomes an assassin and Fletcher acts as her handler. I found Fletcher to be a most interesting character, even though he was not around for most of the book. <br /><br />I liked all the people that surrounded Gin. Finnegan Lane (Finn), Fletcher’s son was a wonderful character. I so wanted Gin to be his love interest, but it was not happening. Finn was a great supporting character. <br /><br />I had trouble believing the attraction between Gin and Donovan Craig. I did not like the way that Donovan treated Gin. I found that his character fell flat for me because of his condescending attitude towards Gin, even though he was alive because of her. <br /><br />The villain was especially evil and scary. I enjoyed the mystery of figuring out who she was and I was pleasantly surprised when I had guessed wrong. I loved the ending and it made me rush out to find the next book in the series Web of Lies. <br /><br /><b>Check out my review on <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com/2011/08/16/feature-author-monday-late-jennifer-esteps-elemental-assassins/" rel="nofollow noopener">Badass Book Reviews</a></b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9889236587278417227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_72974510" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72974510" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/72974510?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Dark UF/Noir UF Fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to  Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books) by: </span>
      Suzi (Gotta Love PNR with a Kick Group Challenge)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=very-dark-read">very-dark-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=southern-setting">southern-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=tough-as-nails-heroine">tough-as-nails-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=magic-noir">magic-noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=character-grieving-loved-one">character-grieving-loved-one</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=latino-hero-or-love-interest">latino-hero-or-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=kickbutt-heroine">kickbutt-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=good-secondary-characters">good-secondary-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72974510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3517368027002708379">Very good and very gritty. Gin is absolutely lethal. Killing someone is just a job to her. Not that she kills just anyone, but if you're on her radar for death, you get dead very quickly. I found her character very credible. I won't deny that I sort of have a fascination with fiction stories about assassins. This is a good one. Estep builds a three-dimensional character here with Gin. She's not evil, but she's not a a saintly person either. How can you be when you kill people for a living? <br/><br/>That'</span>
  <span id="freeText3517368027002708379" style="display:none">Very good and very gritty. Gin is absolutely lethal. Killing someone is just a job to her. Not that she kills just anyone, but if you're on her radar for death, you get dead very quickly. I found her character very credible. I won't deny that I sort of have a fascination with fiction stories about assassins. This is a good one. Estep builds a three-dimensional character here with Gin. She's not evil, but she's not a a saintly person either. How can you be when you kill people for a living? <br /><br />That's where the grays come in. If you knew what some of the folks she's killed have done, then you might not count it as such a loss. Ashland is a place full of dark souls, you see. The whole place is corrupt to varying degrees, except for Donovan Caine. He truly is the only honest man in this place. So imagine the dilemma when they discover an attraction between them. Between the cold-hearted (but warm-pantsed) assassin and the straight arrow cop. Yeah, that makes for quite a conflict.<br /><br />If you like magic noir, definitely check this book out. If you like bad*ss women who know how to get the dirty jobs done, definitely check this out. If you have a problem with women who are a bit callous about sex, you might have a problem with Gin. I'm not big on that trait in a heroine (or a hero for that matter). I did like how she does the pursuing when it comes to Donovan. That was kind of cute. And she can be a bit of a bully when she wants to. I can understand why her character is that way, having lost her family and lived on the streets. It's made her into a hard woman, one who doesn't let anyone make a victim out of her. For all that, she does have a sense of honor. At least someone does in this place. As for Caine, he was a bit self-righteous at times. I totally respect his sense of honor, but I think he needs to open his mind a little and ask the whys instead of just blindly following. I find it hard to believe he was completely oblivious to the corruption in his police department. I think he was just willfully ignoring it. A bad tree cannot produce good fruit and vice versa. If his partner was doing that horrible stuff, why didn't he have a clue? I like that Gin didn't try to defend herself to him. Why should she? She was true to herself, and he had to accept her or leave her. Either way. I like that he can't put her into a box and forget about her either. Too bad Gin can't get this cop out of her mind either. That relationship is fraught with issues.<br /><br />The magic was cool. I liked the concept of elementals, and how many folks in Ashland had elemental magic. I liked the use of runes to identify people, and how it was used to seal magic, if you will. The vampires felt sort of extraneous, but maybe that's because I'm jaded with vampires being in every single urban fantasy series!<br /><br />Overall, this was a very good book. Gin is a very lethal, fascinating character. I didn't like everything about her, but I liked a lot. I loved that she was so bad*ss and capable. She does a lot of the saving, but she also works together with others, so there was balance in that. Donovan is an interesting love interest. It should be entertaining to see where things go with that angel. I also liked the foodie aspects (being a big foodie myself), and the glimpses of Southern life and society. I recommend this book to readers who enjoy enjoy dark, gritty urban fantasy, and tough female leads. I will definitely continue this series!<br /><br /><i> Thanks for recommending this book off my tbr pile, Suzi!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3517368027002708379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_120984338" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120984338" />
    <a title="Ami" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/134600-ami"><img alt="Ami" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485783876p2/134600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120984338?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ami" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ami" href="/user/show/134600-ami">Ami</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781439155431" href="/book/show/7597915-spider-s-bite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal-futuristic">urban-fantasy-paranormal-futuristic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120984338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer891113980213005184"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Okay, let me start with the good ones: (1) The story is set in the "present" world; some of the people have extraordinary talent, magical talent, based on one of the elementals: Fire, Ice, Stone, and Air. It makes it easy to follow because there are no big jargons/words or complicated structure of magical worlds (2) The story is kind of fast-paced of a whodunit plot; someone is killed, our heroine is being bertrayed, her handler is killed, and the whole story is about her finding out th</span>
  <span id="freeText891113980213005184" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br />Okay, let me start with the good ones: (1) The story is set in the "present" world; some of the people have extraordinary talent, magical talent, based on one of the elementals: Fire, Ice, Stone, and Air. It makes it easy to follow because there are no big jargons/words or complicated structure of magical worlds (2) The story is kind of fast-paced of a whodunit plot; someone is killed, our heroine is being bertrayed, her handler is killed, and the whole story is about her finding out the truth (3) I kinda like Gin as a heroine, she is smart and ruthless, a perfect assassin but still sarcastic enough to make me like her (4) I also love Finn, her best friend who can also be seen as Gin's "half" brother by closeness of association.<br /><br />BUT, there are several things that just annoy the HELL out of me, and I can't really get them out of the way to make me love this story more:<br /><br />(1) The repetitive writing is just DRIVING ME INSANE!!!!! First, the way Gin always ends her "fantasy" of Donovan Caine with the word "Mmm". Seriously, after you find this word more than three times, you want to erase the word from your vocabulary forever. That, and the 'cousin' of Mmmm, which is "Hmmm". <br /><br />(2) There are A LOT of unnecessary descriptions of one's look or one's dress; which is totally going nowhere. And what's with the fixation of someone's eye colors? There are repetitive description of Gin's grey eyes, Finn's green eyes, and Caine's hazel eyes. Also this combination of "grey on gold; gold on grey" everytime Caine and Gin look at each other?? Yes, I get it, their eyes are grey, green, and hazel, can we frickin' move on then?!<br /><br />(3) What's with the "concept of repetition in three" since Gin always says "sloppy. sloppy. sloppy" when it comes to her enemy and "slaps slaps slaps" to describe someone being beaten. AND also, emotions should be a mixture of at least 3 things .. "Disgust. Anger. Mistrust. Suspicion. Curiosity." then "Shock. Anger. Disgust. Horror. Resignation.” Yes, one is conflicted, but really, LESS IS MORE!<br /><br />(4) Last but not least, is I HATE DONOVAN CAINE, the supposed to be love interest of Gin. Ms. Estep probably wants to portray him as this one honest person with high idealism. But he comes out as a judgmental, arrogant bastard who thinks that he is better than everyone else. I can get attraction that starts from misunderstanding; look at Elizabeth Bennett and Mr. Darcy. However, Caine doesn't only "misunderstand" Gin, he clearly despises her, and disgusted with the fact that there is some sort of attraction between them. I don't need that kind of hero. Sometimes I wish Gin just kills that a**hole.<br /><br />I might be a little bit too harsh; especially since this is the first book and I rarely fall in love with the first book in a series. However, I don't think it intrigues me enough for book #2 ...</span>
  <a data-text-id="891113980213005184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=big-fucking-nope">big-fucking-nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=fat-kitty-judges-you">fat-kitty-judges-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=annoying-main-character">annoying-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=paranormal-fix">paranormal-fix</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=lust-at-first-sight">lust-at-first-sight</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126635198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18388060300480191504">I picked <i>Spider’s Bite</i> because I wanted to read a good Urban Fantasy. The assassin theme is another major reason that pushed me into it.<br/><br/>What the book description fails to mention is that <i>Spider’s Bite</i> has nothing to do with assassins. At least not my version of an assassin. Jennifer Estep just went on and on with how sexy and deadly Gin is, but never proved it. The deadly part of course. I don’t care about how hot anyone is in the book as long as I get a cool story. In our case, a cool assassin-</span>
  <span id="freeText18388060300480191504" style="display:none">I picked <i>Spider’s Bite</i> because I wanted to read a good Urban Fantasy. The assassin theme is another major reason that pushed me into it.<br><br>What the book description fails to mention is that <i>Spider’s Bite</i> has nothing to do with assassins. At least not my version of an assassin. Jennifer Estep just went on and on with how sexy and deadly Gin is, but never proved it. The deadly part of course. I don’t care about how hot anyone is in the book as long as I get a cool story. In our case, a cool assassin-related story. <br><br>Which I did not get. <br><br>Now don’t get me wrong, I didn’t want it to be perfectly authentic, but I was expecting a bit more effort from Estep. The story and characters ended up being extremely generic.<br><br>Needless to say, I did not enjoy the book an I ended up skimming most of it. The introduction of <i>Spider’s Bite</i> was pretty good. The asylum scene made me think that the rest of the book will continue like that. Of course it never happened.<br><br>Gin’s powers are awesome, but she never uses them because of pride.<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340540i/696898._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Pride. Now that’s a lame excuse. Using those powers would really improve the book if you ask me.<br><br>Gin’s love interest extremely boring. Insta-lust was a turnoff, and the romance was monotonous. <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>The detective reminded me of a Hispanic Dirty Harry, ready to plug anybody who got in his way.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340540i/696899._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They did have sex, but I skipped it because Gin’s way of coming on to the guy was just silly. Estep’s forcing a pair of balls on Gin. I guess this is supposed to be an assassin thing.<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340540i/696900.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story was incredibly generic. Estep’s writing style is mediocre. I won’t be continuing this series.<br><br>Review also posted on<br><a href="http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/2012/11/spiders-bite-elemental-assassin-1.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340428i/696822.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_120970089" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120970089" />
    <a title="Zuleika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3565630-zuleika"><img alt="Zuleika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354364529p2/3565630.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120970089?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zuleika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zuleika" href="/user/show/3565630-zuleika">Zuleika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3565630-zuleika?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3565630-zuleika?shelf=09september">09september</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3565630-zuleika?shelf=urbanfantasy">urbanfantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120970089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6405764797980042358">Meh. That’s kind of how I would describe this book. It was good because it held my attention, I liked the main character and I finished it in one go, but I didn’t feel that connected to the story and I certainly didn’t feel the urge to finish it immediately because I just had to know what happened. So, overall, just meh. <br/><br/>Gin makes a perfect urban fantasy heroine though. She is sarcastic, tough as nails and kicks major butt. I liked her no bullshitting around/ frank attitude (in both knowing her </span>
  <span id="freeText6405764797980042358" style="display:none">Meh. That’s kind of how I would describe this book. It was good because it held my attention, I liked the main character and I finished it in one go, but I didn’t feel that connected to the story and I certainly didn’t feel the urge to finish it immediately because I just had to know what happened. So, overall, just meh. <br /><br />Gin makes a perfect urban fantasy heroine though. She is sarcastic, tough as nails and kicks major butt. I liked her no bullshitting around/ frank attitude (in both knowing her abilities and being honest in her attraction to Detective Donovan) and even though she always remained cool as a cucumber, she still managed to be a sympathic and interesting character. But, while I understand how Ashland is like Gotham/Sin City, after a while it got annoying how every baddy/target were rapists, abusers and/or pedophiles, just so the writer could justify Gin killing them (despite Gin being portrayed as having a very unapologetic view on who/why she kills)<br /><br />I HATED the love story. Listen, I can deal with heroes who start out disliking or even hating the heroines, but Donovan didn’t just hate Gin - He thought she was the scum of the earth and despised her. He didn’t even have any respect for her and he had this crappy holier-than-thou attitude all throughout the book. I kept waiting for him to ‘reform’ and to show her some respect/kindness, but he never did. And if he had any feelings for Gin, they were all drowned out by his self-hate and loathing for being into her. WOW, WHAT A DREAMBOAT. I don’t understand how Gin had any feelings for him at all<br /><br />One more thing: this is such a minor thing and probably something only I find annoying, but three words/phrases were constantly repeated and it DROVE ME INSANE. (sorry for not adding the pages next to the quotes, but I was reading an e-book)<br /><br />1. The word ‘Mmm’<br /><i>-“…until we were both spent and sweaty and satiated. Mmm.”- “…before plunging into the curls at the junction of my thighs. Mmm.”- “…supporting my neck and shoulders. Mmm” “…just breathe in his scent. Mmm.”- “...I wondered if the detective slept nude.<br />Mmm.” </i><br /><br />Everytime Gin was thinking R-rated thoughts/checking out Donovan she had to tack on the word ‘Mmm’ at the end of the sentence. My search function found the word ‘Mmm’ sixteen times. So, for a ‘fun’ drinking game, make sure to take a shot every time that word appears.<br /><br />2. Eye color is very important and therefore MUST be repeated all the time<br /><i>“Sophia’s black eyes met my gray ones.”- “Her wide blue-green eyes met my narrowed gray ones.”- “His amber eyes caught and held my gray ones” -“Our eyes met, gray on gold.” </i>(this one showed up word for word three times)<i>- “he stared into my gray eyes.”- “the frigid chill in my gray eyes” “…and our eyes met. Gold on gray.”- “My eyes met Donovan Caine’s. Gray on gold.”- “my cold, gray eyes.” - “Our gazes met, gray on gold.”</i><br /><br />This one drives me crazy. Gins eyes are gray I GET IT. No need to say it every time her eyes are mentioned. The times when she meets Donovan’s eyes and the phrase: “gray meets gold” or any variation of it was especially annoying.<br /><br />3. Donovan Caine has a LOT of feelings<br /><i>“Emotions flickered in the amber depths, one after another, like lightning bugs winking on and off.Disgust. Anger. Mistrust. Suspicion. Curiosity.” - “Emotions flickered in his golden gaze. Shock. Anger. Disgust. Horror. Resignation.” - “More emotions flashed in his eyes. Desire. Guilt. Hesitation. Need.” - “Emotions flashed in his eyes like lightning.Desire. Want. Need. Guilt.” - “He stared at me, emotions sliding over his face. Desire. Want. Need. Guilt.” - “Emotions flashed in the hazel depths, the way they always did. Weariness, resolve, curiosity.”</i><br /><br />One of my literature pet peeves is when it’s stated that a certain feeling ‘’flashed/raged through his eyes” or any sort of sentence where you can somehow tell exactly how someone is feeling by checking out their eyeballs. I don’t mind it a few times, but after a while it’s like come on…there are more ways of reading emotions then through a ‘flicker in his gaze’. That’s what eyebrows and mouths are for.<br />Also, the way those emotions are all stated one after another gives me the mental image of him pulling a dramatized version of those faces one after another and the mental picture of that makes me LOL (while all of those quotes come from intense/serious scenes)<br /><br />Still, I heard the sequel is loads better (as is usually the case with urbanfantasy series), so I will pick up the next one. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6405764797980042358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2731711732659976646" style="display:none">Welllll, there were some cool things here. I enjoyed the main character enough to go along with the ride, but honestly I didn't really get the love interest guy at all, he didn't really PROVE he was hot and bothered, the writer just kept TELLING me he was, so I didn't really care what happened between them. There were a few leaps in the plot I found a bit disbelieving as well, and I felt the magic of the world, the whole elemental aspect, is SUPER interesting but wasn't exploited enough to feel satisfied at the end.<br /><br />BUT I did like the main characters balls-out attitude and I will pick up the second in the series to see where she goes with the world, because I think some really cool stuff could be done with the elemental magic stuff.     <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1113819977?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781480527751" href="/book/show/17658754-spider-s-bite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1113819977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5002059904855499754">You know...I put reading this book off for some time because of the cover. I mean so often when a book on the Urban Fantasy shelf has an attractive woman on the cover what you actually get is "PNR", that is "ParaNormal Romance".<br/><br/>Good news, not the case here. There is a "touch" of something that will bother some but it's more incidental that a romance usually is. Instead of a "love interest" here we have a "lust interest". Each time our protagonist sees the "subordinate male protagonist" she stops</span>
  <span id="freeText5002059904855499754" style="display:none">You know...I put reading this book off for some time because of the cover. I mean so often when a book on the Urban Fantasy shelf has an attractive woman on the cover what you actually get is "PNR", that is "ParaNormal Romance".<br /><br />Good news, not the case here. There is a "touch" of something that will bother some but it's more incidental that a romance usually is. Instead of a "love interest" here we have a "lust interest". Each time our protagonist sees the "subordinate male protagonist" she stops and "daydreams" about hot sex with him...even though he's vowed to bring her "to justice" or possibly kill her.<br /><br />And, there is one heavy sex scene.<br /><br />Well, he doesn't know it's "her" per se, he simply knows that it was an assassin "called" The Spider.<br /><br />Yes, our heroine is an assassin...a truly nasty one. She claims to be the most feared assassin in the South. She also has a true love for the burgers at the Bar-B-Que place she works from.<br /><br />As I've said about other assassin books I'm surprised at how much I really liked this book. I plan to follow the series up and if you approach it knowingly (you know advisedly that there is some sex and it's about a professional killer) you may like it.<br /><br />It worries me a little but I did. Recommended, with caveat. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5002059904855499754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1508249560" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1508249560" />
    <a title="Ashley Marie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie"><img alt="Ashley Marie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471208025p2/29787548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_1018692496" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1018692496" />
    <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans"><img alt="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587115780p2/7298986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1018692496?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans">✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8176904-spider-s-bite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=cool-kick-ass-chicks-ltd">cool-kick-ass-chicks-ltd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1018692496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4104421770125982678">When I started reading Spider’s Bite the series was already in its 12th instalment. The question was, would I get hooked and want to read the whole series in one go? Well that’s pretty much what I’ve been doing for the past week! Granted, one instalment (Tangled Threads, #4 in the series) almost had me give up on the series but I’m still going along with it at the moment (more on that in reviews to come).<br/><br/>Well, about Spider’s Bite. I think what I liked more about the book is the idea of a female </span>
  <span id="freeText4104421770125982678" style="display:none">When I started reading Spider’s Bite the series was already in its 12th instalment. The question was, would I get hooked and want to read the whole series in one go? Well that’s pretty much what I’ve been doing for the past week! Granted, one instalment (Tangled Threads, #4 in the series) almost had me give up on the series but I’m still going along with it at the moment (more on that in reviews to come).<br /><br />Well, about Spider’s Bite. I think what I liked more about the book is the idea of a female assassin with “elemental” magic. I thought the premise was original and intriguing, which got me hooked right away. I love Gin’s character, even though she could have done with a lot more snark to spice things up a bit. She’s a ruthless killer but her character is still very loveable. I love that she is so straight-forward and always speaks her mind. She is confident, self-assured and when she wants something (or <b>someone</b> like Donovan Caine) she goes for it. She is unapologetic about who she is and what she does, she has no qualms about being an assassin. Gotta love that! I think Gin Blanco just made it to the top 5 in my favourite kick-butt heroines list!<br /><br />As for the other characters in Spider’s Bite, I pretty much liked them all (including the bad guys!). Finn (love him!), the Deveraux sisters (lots of potential there), Fletcher… Donovan Caine I’m not too sure about. His high morals bore me to death and he is so self-righteous and insensitive that he makes me want to scream most of the time. I really have no idea what Gin sees in him besides his “fuck potential.” I’m curious as to where this attraction is going. Nowhere probably but I guess we’ll have to wait for the next instalments to find out.<br /><br />As a whole, I found Spider’s Bite to be quite enjoyable. I was a bit taken aback at first because I thought it was a bit light on the fantasy side of the story. I’ve just read the last instalment in the Kate Daniels series, then the whole Descent series (both being urban fantasy heavy weights) so it took me some time to adjust. Don’t get me wrong, there is fantasy here (magic, vampires, dwarves…), it’s just that I wasn’t swept away by the world building. Still, Spider’s Bite is well-written and entertaining. <br /><br />I definitely want to find out what happens next so I’ll get my hands on the next instalment right away :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4104421770125982678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1506656736" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1506656736" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14323468-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434090906p2/14323468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

      <a href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=mine">mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=gr2016">gr2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1506656736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4979436648708466394"><blockquote>
  <i>No matter how bad people were, no matter what evil they committed, or who they fucked over, nobody ever really believed death was coming for them, courtesy of an assassin like me.<br/>Until it was too late.</i>
</blockquote> <p>There are two words for why you must read this book: FEMALE ASSASSIN. <br/>Yip, a kick-ass knife wielding heroine, who doesn’t take s#$t from anyone. My kind of girl.</p> <p>Gin Blanco, known as the Spider, is an assassin. She is also a stone elemental. Elementals can create, control and manipulate ice, s</p></span>
  <span id="freeText4979436648708466394" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>No matter how bad people were, no matter what evil they committed, or who they fucked over, nobody ever really believed death was coming for them, courtesy of an assassin like me.<br />Until it was too late.</i>
</blockquote> <p>There are two words for why you must read this book: FEMALE ASSASSIN. <br />Yip, a kick-ass knife wielding heroine, who doesn’t take s#$t from anyone. My kind of girl.</p> <p>Gin Blanco, known as the Spider, is an assassin. She is also a stone elemental. Elementals can create, control and manipulate ice, stone, air or fire. And I loved Gin’s magic with stone, especially the fact that she could change her skin to stone. She also has a minor ability with ice, and can create objects like knifes ;-) </p> <blockquote>
  <i>“You and those fucking knives,” Brutus muttered and yanked the blade out of his shoulder socket. “Get a real weapon. Get a gun.”<br />“Guns are for people who don’t have the guts or skill to use a blade.” </i>
</blockquote> <p>When a job goes wrong, and Gin is double crossed, her handler, who saved her when she was young, killed, she sets out to get revenge. She has no problem with violence, and my bloodthirsty heart was very happy with her methods ;-) I really loved how skilled Gin is, and that even though she comes across as coldhearted, she is still vulnerable when it comes to those she cares for. </p> <p>The plot of the story was strong, and action-packed. I loved the secondary characters, especially Finn, the son of her handler, who was very funny and charming, and I really liked that he never judged her for what she does for a living. </p> <p>Then there was the little background of Gin that was revealed, how her family was murdered years ago by a fire elemental, and Gin captured and tortured. I can’t wait to find out more about what happened and who was responsible for their murders. </p> <p>I’m not sure whether Detective Donovan Caine, who Gin has some very explosive chemistry with, is going to be a possible love interest. I can’t really see them working as a couple, seeing as he despises what she does for a living. I will have to wait and see. </p> <p>I really enjoyed this book. This was a great and strong beginning to a series that I think I’m going to love. I adore strong heroines, and Gin is awesome! </p> <p>A must read for all UF fans. </p></span>
  <a data-text-id="4979436648708466394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1443257866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16669297525448169715">3.5 Well, this was better than I expected.<br/><br/>So, when I started reading this, I expected the same old PNR, the detectives, the cases, the "superpowers" and so on. And you know what? It was exactly like that.<br/><br/>What did surprise me though was the story. I liked the mystery from this book. And I also appreciated the fact that the assassin wasn't that squishy little girl, who was good but had no other choice but to become a killer. Nope, "Spider" actually liked what she did. Ok, true, she only killed bad</span>
  <span id="freeText16669297525448169715" style="display:none">3.5 Well, this was better than I expected.<br /><br />So, when I started reading this, I expected the same old PNR, the detectives, the cases, the "superpowers" and so on. And you know what? It was exactly like that.<br /><br />What did surprise me though was the story. I liked the mystery from this book. And I also appreciated the fact that the assassin wasn't that squishy little girl, who was good but had no other choice but to become a killer. Nope, "Spider" actually liked what she did. Ok, true, she only killed bad people, but she still liked it. And hey, if you become a killer, I would expect you to like what you do.<br /><br />So yup, I appreciated the "real-ness" of this story. I even liked the characters. The writing wasn't too bad either (although it took me a while to get in the story). Yup, a pretty nice book, all in all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16669297525448169715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1920561747" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1920561747?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=when-words-collide">when-words-collide</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=public-library">public-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>,
