        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1920561747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5179066426496514705">I decided to start this series as the author will be attending a conference that I am registered for this summer. I like to have a feel for the work of the featured guests before the event.<br/><br/>If you are enamoured of urban fantasy, as I am, I would recommend this book to you. If, on the other hand, you find UF tiresome, pass this series by. For those of us who enjoy the genre, this is an acceptable series, with a number of good ideas.<br/><br/>Good ideas: (1) A female assassin. With magical powers, although s</span>
  <span id="freeText5179066426496514705" style="display:none">I decided to start this series as the author will be attending a conference that I am registered for this summer. I like to have a feel for the work of the featured guests before the event.<br /><br />If you are enamoured of urban fantasy, as I am, I would recommend this book to you. If, on the other hand, you find UF tiresome, pass this series by. For those of us who enjoy the genre, this is an acceptable series, with a number of good ideas.<br /><br />Good ideas: (1) A female assassin. With magical powers, although she tries not to rely on them. (2) An interesting elemental magic scheme. (3) Gin (our assassin friend) is confident, competent &amp; doesn’t even pretend that she’s a loner. She has friends who are like family &amp; freely admits it.<br /><br />The stuff that didn’t work so well for me? (1) The repetition. How many times do we need to be told where Gin carries all of her knives? Or how much she loves all of her knives? (2) The novel was filled with UF clichés, e.g. the main character has a tragic &amp; damaging past (shades of Batman), she has a “code” (à la Dexter or Spademan in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17834909.Shovel_Ready__Spademan___1_" title="Shovel Ready (Spademan, #1) by Adam Sternbergh" rel="nofollow noopener">Shovel Ready</a>). (3)<i> Of course</i> she is romantically interested in a policeman, he is as self-righteous as she is pragmatic, and every time she lays eyes on him all she can think about is sex <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(but her little feelings are hurt when they eventually have sex &amp; he still dislikes her). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The set-up of Gin’s world is a little grittier and darker than I would normally choose. Sexual situations are just part of the background (lots of prostitutes &amp; their clients) and often described more graphically than other UF series that I have read. I realize that it is just part of Gin’s “wrong side of the tracks” world, but it grated on me a bit.<br /><br />Still, I liked the book and will continue with the series, both to see if Gin can “go straight” with her restaurant business (I assuming not entirely or the series is named wrong) and if she does, whether Detective Caine will unbend a bit and meet her in the middle.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5179066426496514705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1625658206?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷" href="/user/show/45487389-layla-praise-the-sun">Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1625658206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13336281517099831499">Buddy read at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a><br/><br/><b>My name is Gin, and I kill people</b><br/><br/><b>Without long introductions</b>, Spider's Bite throws us right into action as we witness Gin, the protagonist, on an assignment to eliminate Evelyn, a shrink in Ashland Asylum with dark secrets and we get a glance at Gin's working methods. <br/>Then Gin is double-crossed on her next suspiciously lucrative and easy assignment and her handler is brutally tortured and killed. <br/>Now she is out for revenge.<br/><br/>The <b>story is set</b> in Ashland, a city</span>
  <span id="freeText13336281517099831499" style="display:none">Buddy read at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a><br /><br /><b>My name is Gin, and I kill people</b><br /><br /><b>Without long introductions</b>, Spider's Bite throws us right into action as we witness Gin, the protagonist, on an assignment to eliminate Evelyn, a shrink in Ashland Asylum with dark secrets and we get a glance at Gin's working methods. <br />Then Gin is double-crossed on her next suspiciously lucrative and easy assignment and her handler is brutally tortured and killed. <br />Now she is out for revenge.<br /><br />The <b>story is set</b> in Ashland, a city divided in Northtown, home to the monetary, magical and social elite, and Southtown, the rough part of town belonging to vampire hookers and junkies. <br />There are fantasy creatures like dwarfs, giants, elementals and vampires. <br /><br />Gin, the <b>heroine</b>, is strong, just doesn't take shit from anyone and she seems brutal and cold on the outside, but she carries her package and Estep manages to make her quite likeable anyways. It just feels so good when she doesn't let the bullies bully her. <br /><br />Besides being a preferrably knife wielding assassin, Gin is also a stone and ice elemental, able to crumble bricks, crack concrete, make her skin as hard as marble and create ice cubes or other little objects like knifes. <br /><br />Then there is <b>Finn</b>. He is the son of Gin's handler, investment banker and computer expert. <br />If that doesn't make him shady enough for you yet, he also happens to excel at females and fashion, so he is mainly in charge of calling in favors and doing all the intelligence work. <br /><br />While Gin and Finn were absolutely refreshing together <br /><br /><b>Been there. Done you</b>, <br /><br />I had my issues to warm up to <b>Donovan Caine</b>, morally superior detective and potential love interest for Gin. He was a bit too stick in the sphincter and self-righteous for my liking, and Gin referring to him as "Mmm" 13 times in the book didn't help. <br /><br />In general, there were <b>too many repetitions</b>, for instance when Gin tells us 22 times about her gray eyes. Ok, I get it, your eyes are neither khaki green nor sheet brown, now please move on. <br /><br />Apart from the repetitions, I had a great time reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6611038.Spider_s_Bite__Elemental_Assassin___1_" title="Spider's Bite (Elemental Assassin, #1) by Jennifer Estep" rel="nofollow noopener">Spider's Bite</a> though, and I will definitely read the next installments in the series. <br /><br />If you love stories featuring powerful assassins with a tragic past like I do, you should definitely check this out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13336281517099831499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1529603079" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1529603079" />
    <a title="Pippa DaCosta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23314834-pippa-dacosta"><img alt="Pippa DaCosta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499153245p2/23314834.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1529603079?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pippa DaCosta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pippa DaCosta" href="/user/show/23314834-pippa-dacosta">Pippa DaCosta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1529603079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4623871790995119345">If you know me, or you've read any of my work, you know I love books that walk an edgy line. I like a bit of grit and dirt in my urban fantasy reads. Nothing too squeaky clean or ditzy. The dirt, for me, makes a series feel more real. It gives the characters genuine depth. If they're gleefully hacking of monster heads and not getting kneed in the balls while having their morals challenged, then I struggle to fully believe that our main characters are real and not cardboard cutouts. There was no </span>
  <span id="freeText4623871790995119345" style="display:none">If you know me, or you've read any of my work, you know I love books that walk an edgy line. I like a bit of grit and dirt in my urban fantasy reads. Nothing too squeaky clean or ditzy. The dirt, for me, makes a series feel more real. It gives the characters genuine depth. If they're gleefully hacking of monster heads and not getting kneed in the balls while having their morals challenged, then I struggle to fully believe that our main characters are real and not cardboard cutouts. There was no risk of that here. <br /><br />Gin is as bad-ass as they come without being unlikeable. (You can't have an assassin that gleefully kills with no morals, not in fantasy land. They have to have a reason to do good somewhere in there, or you end up reading about a psychopath). I love that she knows exactly what she wants and she's not going to let anyone stand in her way. Take the detective, for example. If you're expecting the gentle, slow romantic build up and the swoony, doe-eyed moments, you won't get any of that here. Gin doesn't much like the detective or his choices, but she likes what she sees and she's gonna bag herself some of that man-candy. The quick and dirty f*ck in the supply closet tells you what you need to know. Gin doesn't waste time. <br /><br />We have a tightly plotted typical UF. Gin's handler is murdered. We follow her as she tries to figure out by whom and why. There's nothing groundbreaking here, to be fair, but it's the voice I adored. That raw, edgy, no BS kinda character that's the perfect antidote to TSTL heroines.<br /><br />I'm looking forward to the next in the series...</span>
  <a data-text-id="4623871790995119345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_995498471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/995498471" />
    <a title="Beth The Vampire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22241496-beth-the-vampire"><img alt="Beth The Vampire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483516030p2/22241496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/995498471?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth The Vampire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth The Vampire" href="/user/show/22241496-beth-the-vampire">Beth The Vampire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=series-1st">series-1st</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=sos-challenge-2017">sos-challenge-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer995498471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6471098249364565381"><b>My name is Gin, and I kill people.</b><br/><br/>Okay, this book was good. Really good.<br/><br/>I don't know what I was expecting really, but the blurb sounded good, so why not give it a go. Also I was completing this as part of the Serious Overload of Series 2017 series read.<br/><br/>Gin is an assassin, and a very good one at that. She is known by the name Spider, but most don't think that a girl could be capable of the death that follows this assassin around. Their mistake really. As well as being a skilled killer for hire, G</span>
  <span id="freeText6471098249364565381" style="display:none"><b>My name is Gin, and I kill people.</b><br /><br />Okay, this book was good. Really good.<br /><br />I don't know what I was expecting really, but the blurb sounded good, so why not give it a go. Also I was completing this as part of the Serious Overload of Series 2017 series read.<br /><br />Gin is an assassin, and a very good one at that. She is known by the name Spider, but most don't think that a girl could be capable of the death that follows this assassin around. Their mistake really. As well as being a skilled killer for hire, Gin is also a Stone elemental, meaning that she has an affinity with, and can harness the power of stone. She has a little knowledge of ice magic as well, which can come in handy when picking locks, chilling drinks....or stabbing people in the neck.<br /><br />So after a week long assignment, Gin is called by her handler for another job, which is worth quite a bit of money. So, reluctantly she takes it, but it turns out to be a set up, and Gin finds out that she is the pawn in a much larger game. With her life in danger, Gin finds an unlikely alley in good cop Donovan Caine, and they also have quite a bit of chemistry as well. With the help of her hander's banker son, Finn, Gin is determined to track down who has placed those she loves in danger, and who took the life of the person who meant the most.<br /><br /><b>No matter how bad people were, no matter what evil they committed, or who they fucked over, nobody really believed death was coming for them, courtesy of an assassin like me.<br />Until it was too late.</b><br /><br />I found the story quite compelling, and rarely dull. Gin is an amazing protagonist, because she is not a good guy, but she's not exactly a bad guy either. She is strong, and determined, and in the end she gets what she wants. When her and Caine come to realise their mutual attraction, Gin doesn't step back and let him take over, she remains in control. There are no alpha males here...unless you count Gin. Even Gin isn't silly enough to believe in love at first sight or anything silly like that. She just acknowledges good old lust, and why does it have to be more than that?<br /><br />The characters were all great, even those who only get limited page time, such as the enigmatic Mab Monroe, who essentially rules the city with her money and power. She didn't speak a word, but her presence in a scene was enough to tell me what I needed. Caine was your typical good cop, but in the end I think he realised that there is no black and while, only shades of grey. Finn and Gin's relationship was very much like a brother and sister, despite no blood relation, and very different ways of living. Some of their back and forth was very amusing, and they had great chemistry. I loved the goth troll as well. Just the imagery alone was amusing.<br /><br />One of the small issues I will note though is Gin's rumination towards the start that she wants to take revenge on those she loved who have been killed, even though she essentially kills people for a living. It's like the author is trying to justify it in a way, and while this would have to have been mentioned at some point, it comes up a few times and I kind of just wanted Gin to get over it. Yeah, she kills people, and yeah she wants to kill those who have hurt her, just like she may have hurt others by her illegal dealings, but she doesn't need to say more than that. It may make her a hypocrite, but who isn't these days?<br /><br />The ending was set up so well for a sequel, and I'm really looking forward to it. If this is the series I will be reading a lot of this year, then this is going to be a great year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6471098249364565381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4378045356615163074" style="display:none">This is my new audio book - I've listened for an hour so far and haven't stopped :) I'm intrigued!<br /><br />I finished this weekend. I enjoyed the story - an insight into an assassin and how she became one and what drives her. Strong female protagonist is always welcome.   <b>
    <i>“My name is Gin, and I kill people.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404660085ra/10269407.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Spider's Bite was awesome! A great book with lots of action, blood, killing, sorrow, laughter, even a hot sexy sex scene. I immediately took a liking to it, and i was curious for how the book would turn out, and man was i glad i read it. I don't understand why i waited so long to read it?! I love reading about female warriors, and this female lead is an assassin, so that itself should say something. <br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I’m the Spider. Surely you’ve heard of m</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText9651795121866351188" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“My name is Gin, and I kill people.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404660085ra/10269407.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Spider's Bite was awesome! A great book with lots of action, blood, killing, sorrow, laughter, even a hot sexy sex scene. I immediately took a liking to it, and i was curious for how the book would turn out, and man was i glad i read it. I don't understand why i waited so long to read it?! I love reading about female warriors, and this female lead is an assassin, so that itself should say something. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I’m the Spider. Surely you’ve heard of me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>My casting:</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404657178i/10269096.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Emotions were for those too weak to turn them off.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The book follows Gin Blanco, or the Spider—the most feared assassin in the South. She's ruthless, fast, dangerous and sassy. Most of her kills are fast and mostly painless, unless you get on her really bad side, like the villains in this book does. The bad guys strike at her personal, attacking the people she cares about- and now she's out for revenge. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404655632ra/10268883.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Easy was for people too weak to suck it up and do what needed to be done. <br>And I wasn’t weak. Not anymore.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Gin has been through hell when she was a kid, and had to live on the street for months. Luckily Fletcher - who becomes her mentor and father-figure, took her in when she was 13 years old and trained her. When she finds him dead after being setup on a mission, Gin is filled with rage, fury, pain, panic and she feels lost.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404655632ra/10268882.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Death was a release, in so many ways. An end to suffering. An escape to something else. What that something else was, I didn’t know. Maybe heaven. Maybe hell. Maybe nothing at all. But I doubted it could be any worse than some of the things I’d seen and done in my lifetime.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404656328ra/10268960.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Good thing she's patient, and smart. She starts making plans for catching Fletcher's killers, with the help of Finn (Fletcher's son) and Detective Donovan Caine, who hates her guts, specially when he starts to feel for her.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You can work with me—or you can wade through the blood and bodies after I'm done.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404657111ra/10269091.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Gin is up against a powerful Air elemental, who likes to tutoure people. Gin herself, has two elementals: Stone elemental and Ice elemental. Though, her Ice elementals isn't that powerful. She doesn't use her powers on the job/missions unless she absolutely have to. She doesn't want to depend on her powers, because who knows, one day they might let her down. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>No matter how bad people were, no matter what evil they committed, or who they fucked over, nobody ever really believed death was coming for them, courtesy of an assassin like me.<br>Until it was too late. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404657111ra/10269092.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Gin is an awesome character to read about! She funny, curious, intelligent, strong, and a goddamn good friend. She doesn't take crap, and if you betray her, you're dead. Gin doesn't necessary love her job, but she's good at it, so why quit? <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Trouble has a habit of finding me. And I have a habit of dealing with it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404657823ra/10269197.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It's good money, and in a way exciting. She's fantastic at hiding, even in public, and she loves her knives. Oh, and she loves to cook! Gin's never afraid, but she does fear for her friends, specially Finn, who is all she has left. Being weak isn't an option for Gin, so being an assassin helps her feel powerful and not weak.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"But don’t worry, detective. I’ll let you be the good cop. I’m so much better at being the bad guy anyway.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404657823ra/10269198.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Detective Donovan Caine is a good coop. Honest, kind, strong, loyal. He's fighting against his attraction for Gin, so he's a bit grumpy, though i understand his reasons for wanting to hate her. I mean, she did kill his partner and she's an assassin after all. Donovan tries his best to save innocent, and it goes against all his instincts to help Gin and Finn, but he want justice so he has no choice.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Emotions flickered in the amber depths, one after another, like lightning bugs winking on and off.Disgust. Anger. Mistrust. Suspicion. Curiosity. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404660085ra/10269408.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Put those on.”<br>“Handcuffs. Kinky. But I prefer to have a bit more freedom during sex. Don’t you?” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>So, you're probably wondering why i didn't give this book more stars. Well, for one, it has a hell of a lot of information, which can be at times boring. Another is the constantly repetitiveness of "Mmm” and “Gold on gray” when her eyes met Donovan’s “hazel eyes” . Or how enemies were always “Sloppy, sloppy, sloppy”. The book was simply dragged out to long.. It should have been shorten a bit. Yet another thing i didn't like was the fact that Donovan was human.. I know right?! I'm weird. I love dominant alpha males, and even though the coop is cool and all, he is still soooo... normal? boring? I wished he was more mysterious and dangerous, so let's hope that changes in the next book. I have a fantasy where he's an werewolf, so i can always hope, i guess :P (never mind that werewolf is not even mentioned in the book) lol <br><b>Rate: 3.5 stars. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9651795121866351188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_123687840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123687840" />
    <a title="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck"><img alt="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472332781p2/4268461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123687840?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" href="/user/show/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck">Emanuela ~plastic duck~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8176904-spider-s-bite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123687840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11874973678111217365">2.5 stars.<br/><br/>I liked the setting: a city in the hand of a powerful and ruthless woman and magic. There are giants, dwarves, vampires but the most fascinating creatures have their own magic which is influenced by an element (Fire, Air, Ice and Stone), even if they do not all possess the same skills in handling it. The non-human creatures are not invincible and irresistible, they're more or less ordinary people, each of them struggling to live their lives in this dark place. We don't know why the wor</span>
  <span id="freeText11874973678111217365" style="display:none">2.5 stars.<br /><br />I liked the setting: a city in the hand of a powerful and ruthless woman and magic. There are giants, dwarves, vampires but the most fascinating creatures have their own magic which is influenced by an element (Fire, Air, Ice and Stone), even if they do not all possess the same skills in handling it. The non-human creatures are not invincible and irresistible, they're more or less ordinary people, each of them struggling to live their lives in this dark place. We don't know why the world is like this, maybe we'll learn something more as the series goes on, but it's fine for me when the author doesn't dump too much information in the first book of a series.<br /><br />Once I said that, I must more or less complain about everything else. <br /><br />The heroine is strong, she has endured a lot in her life and she takes her fate in her hands and fights her own battles alone. She has a good love-me-or-leave-me attitude, but I didn't like her. It's as if she's trying too hard to be a kick-ass heroine.<br /><br />The hero, detective Donovan Caine. Is there a hero? At one point Gin (the heroine) asks him: "Why are you here?" The hero and me had the same answer: "Fuck if I know!" What's the point in writing a hero Gin can't resist if we don't know why (apart from his gold tell-tale eyes)? I think it could have been more interesting if Donovan Caine had asked for Gin's help first and not the contrary, because at the end we find that she could have clearly done everything by herself, he was like a dog on a leash, always following her, I don't even think he had ONE idea. He is even seduced by Gin! <br />Maybe it's me. Maybe I'm wrong in loving alpha heroes.<br /><br />Then there were a lot of repetitions, the action was good but written with a chronometer in hand and the "gold on gray" line became a joke.<br /><br />I think I am going to read the second book because I like corrupted cities like Ashland and I think the series deserves a second chance (I hope the detective finally becomes a man).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11874973678111217365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_105239036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105239036" />
    <a title="Christina " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2621042-christina"><img alt="Christina " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302034398p2/2621042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105239036?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina " href="/user/show/2621042-christina">Christina </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2621042-christina?shelf=uf">uf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105239036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11603188261624383126">3.5 stars.This was a pretty good UF book, and I plan on following the rest of this series.<br/><br/>I liked the unconventional, humane assassin that features as the protagonist in this story. It's a credit to the author's skill that she can create and pull off a character that,while believable and true to her profession's nature,can incite sympathy and respect in the reader.<br/>Gin is smart,sarcastic, tough-as-nails,ruthless and unapologetic,but not the standard of catty know-it-all that seems to plague the g</span>
  <span id="freeText11603188261624383126" style="display:none">3.5 stars.This was a pretty good UF book, and I plan on following the rest of this series.<br /><br />I liked the unconventional, humane assassin that features as the protagonist in this story. It's a credit to the author's skill that she can create and pull off a character that,while believable and true to her profession's nature,can incite sympathy and respect in the reader.<br />Gin is smart,sarcastic, tough-as-nails,ruthless and unapologetic,but not the standard of catty know-it-all that seems to plague the genre. She isn't exactly humble either, though.Rather,conscious of her exact strengths and honest about them.<br /><br />This is very much Gin's story, and so Estep's universe comes through vividly in her particular brand of commentary and worldview.Therefore,situations and/or explanations that might have seemed recited and stiff, are infused with a jagged,world-weary tint. <br /><br />The only thing that bothered me was that judgmental, sanctimonious @$$ of a love interest, Detective Donovan Caine.<br />I couldn't, for the life of me, fathom their attraction. I might have dismissed it as simple lust, or a desire to live dangerously (which seems to be the deal on the detective's case. The detective's case. Ha.),but Gin implies a far deeper attachment on her part.She doesn't seem the sort to pine after <i>anyone</i>, but I still hope she'll not pull a Georgina in the next one,or I'll be very disappointed. :p<br /><br />Oh,and also, a small thing, that got pretty annoying by the end: what's with all the inner monologue "mmm"s in every other page? LOL <i>So</i> weird.<br /><br />All in all, a good, alternative sort of story, with interesting characters and lots of potential.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11603188261624383126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZxWi3ixe40ljM9jV6s/IK8gSdOpmo21T2yG7xvomOlC9ftYGpPqfMjXUrC2MNyNw2PPmVOuVPj4nVpqeUkDevA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  <span id="freeText2412981371208124101" style="display:none">Jennifer Estep is a New York Times, USA Today, and international bestselling author, prowling the streets of her imagination in search of her next fantasy idea.
